## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics (growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of a population state P, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population growth/decline models in ecology and demography. With only (t, P) available, plausible structures include per-capita growth laws r(t, P) multiplied by P, density dependence, Allee effects, and time-varying (e.g., seasonal) forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (constant per-capita growth/decline)
- Affine time-varying per-capita rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (trend in environment or demography)
- Quadratic density dependence (Verhulst logistic ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth)
- Logistic ODE in carrying-capacity parameterization: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (self-limitation with K ~ 1/c1)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (nonlinear crowding response)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (logarithmic decrease of per-capita growth with size)
- Ricker-type continuous crowding: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (exponential suppression at high density)
- Richards-type generalized logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2)**c3 (flexible sigmoidal approach to capacity)
- Strong Allee effect (threshold) with capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth below threshold and above capacity)
- Saturating recruitment minus linear mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P / (P + c1) - c2 * P (resource-limited recruitment with proportional loss)
- Seasonally forced density dependence: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (periodic environment affects growth rate)
- Harvesting/removal (constant yield): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (density-dependent growth with constant extraction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt is proportional to P (near-linear through origin), it suggests constant per-capita rate (births-deaths independent of density).
- A negative P**2 contribution (or P*(1-c*P)) indicates a finite carrying capacity due to crowding/resource limitation.
- A log(c/P) factor implies Gompertz-like regulation where relative growth decreases roughly linearly with log(P).
- An exp(-c*P) multiplier indicates rapidly increasing suppression at high density (crowding effects that strengthen faster than polynomial).
- A (P - c) factor (especially multiplied by P) indicates an Allee threshold: growth becomes negative below a critical population size.
- Explicit sin(c*t + c) modulation points to seasonal forcing or cyclic environmental variability affecting per-capita growth.
- A coefficient that decays like exp(-c*t) suggests gradual environmental deterioration or improving control/harvest over time.
- A constant subtraction term (−c) in dP_dt corresponds to fixed-yield harvesting/removal independent of population size.
- A rational form P/(P+c) indicates saturating recruitment or resource uptake: marginal gains diminish as P grows.
- Replacing P with P**c in density dependence (theta-logistic) signals nonlinear crowding where regulation turns on sharply or gently depending on exponent.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG4)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P/(c4 + exp(-c5*(-c6 + P)))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []

I need to analyze whether any candidate can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT):

$$GT = 0.1728(1 - P/48.55)P + \frac{0.1728 \cdot P}{1 + \exp(-1.524(-0.924 + P))}$$

Simplifying:
$$GT = 0.1728P - 0.003559P^2 + \frac{0.1728P}{1 + \exp(-1.524P + 1.408)}$$

The GT has three structural components:
1. A **linear term** in P: $c \cdot P$
2. A **quadratic term** in P: $c \cdot P^2$
3. A **sigmoidal term**: $\frac{c \cdot P}{1 + \exp(-aP + b)}$

The sigmoidal term $\frac{P}{1+\exp(-aP+b)}$ is a specific nonlinear function that cannot be replicated by polynomials, rational functions, `Max`, `log`, `cos`, `sin`, `1/(polynomial)^n`, or simple exponentials divided by P.

Let me check each candidate's basis functions against this sigmoid:

**Key structural requirement:** The GT contains $\frac{P}{1+\exp(\text{linear in }P)}$, which is a logistic-type sigmoid multiplied by P. This is a fundamentally different basis function from:
- $P/(P^4 c + 1)$ — rational function
- $P/\text{Max}(0, P^2 c + 1)^5$ — rational-like
- $P/(P^c \cdot c + 1)^5$ — power-law rational
- $\exp(cP)/P$ — exponential/P
- $\log(1 + c\exp(cP))$ — softplus-like
- $\cos(ct)$, $\sin(ct)$ — trigonometric in t
- $P/(P+c)$ — simple rational
- $\log(P c + 1)/\sqrt{P}$ — log-sqrt combination

None of these basis functions can exactly equal $\frac{P}{1+\exp(-aP+b)}$ for all P. The sigmoid function is linearly independent from all polynomial, rational, power-law, logarithmic, and simple exponential functions.

Let me verify a few candidates more carefully:

**Candidates with $\exp(cP)/P$ terms (4,5,6,7):** $c\exp(aP)/P$ grows exponentially for large P, while the sigmoid term approaches a constant times P. These cannot match.

**Candidates with $\log(1+c\exp(...)$ (1,8,15):** Candidate 15 has $\log(c_5\exp(Pc_6\sin(c_7 t+c_8))+1)$ — this depends on t, and even setting the t-dependence to make it static, $\log(c\exp(aP)+1)$ is a softplus, not $P/(1+\exp(-aP))$. These are different functions.

**Candidates with $P/(P+c)$ (16,21):** $P/(P+c)$ approaches 1 for large P, while the sigmoid approaches P. Not equivalent.

**Candidates with $P \cdot \text{Max}(0, P+c)$ (13,14):** This is piecewise linear/quadratic, not sigmoidal.

**Candidate 10:** Has $(P^{c_7} c_8 + 1)^{c_9}$ — a generalized power function, not a sigmoid.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain the essential sigmoid basis function $\frac{P}{1+\exp(-aP+b)}$ that appears in the GT. All candidates use fundamentally different nonlinear building blocks (rational functions, power laws, trigonometric functions, simple exponentials, logarithms) that are linearly independent from the logistic sigmoid.
